## Summary

The Kubernetes informer cache event handler chain spans two main repositories (`kubernetes/kubernetes` and `kubernetes/client-go`) and flows through these key layers:

### Complete Chain (API Server → Informer Cache → User Handlers)

1. **etcd3 Storage** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/watcher.go`): `watcher.Watch()` creates a `watchChan` that calls the etcd client's `Watch()`, parses raw etcd events via `parseEvent()`, and sends them through `incomingEventChan` → `processEvents()` → `resultChan` (implementing `watch.Interface`)

2. **Cacher** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go`): `Cacher` wraps etcd3 with an in-memory `watchCache`. It creates a `cache.Reflector` (from client-go) with a `listerWatcher` backed by etcd3 storage. `watchCache.processEvent()` → `cacher.processEvent()` → `dispatchEvents()` → `dispatchEvent()` → `cacheWatcher.sendWatchCacheEvent()` → `result` channel

3. **HTTP Watch Handler** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/`): `ListResource()` → `serveWatchHandler()` → `WatchServer.HandleHTTP()` reads from `ResultChan()` and writes chunked HTTP responses

4. **Client REST** (`rest/request.go`, `rest/watch/decoder.go`): `Request.Watch()` → `newStreamWatcher()` creates a `StreamWatcher` with a `Decoder` that decodes framed watch events from the HTTP stream

5. **ListWatch** (`tools/cache/listwatch.go`): `ListWatch` implements `ListerWatcher`, bridging the REST client to the reflector

"func (f *DeltaFIFO) Pop(process PopProcessFunc) (interface{}, error) {\n        f.lock.Lock()\n        defer f.lock.Unlock()\n        for {\n                for len(f.queue) == 0 {\n                        // When the queue is empty, invocation of Pop() is blocked until new item is enqueued.\n                        // When Close() is called, the f.closed is set and the condition is broadcasted.\n                        // Which causes this loop to continue and return from the Pop().\n                        if f.closed {\n                                return nil, ErrFIFOClosed\n                        }\n\n                        f.cond.Wait()\n                }\n                isInInitialList := !f.hasSynced_locked()\n                id := f.queue[0]\n                f.queue = f.queue[1:]\n                depth := len(f.queue)\n                if f.initialPopulationCount > 0 {\n                        f.initialPopulationCount--\n                }\n                item, ok := f.items[id]\n                if !ok {\n                        // This should never happen\n                        klog.Errorf(\"Inconceivable! %q was in f.queue but not f.items; ignoring.\", id)\n                        continue\n                }\n                delete(f.items, id)\n                // Only log traces if the queue depth is greater than 10 and it takes more than\n                // 100 milliseconds to process one item from the queue.\n                // Queue depth never goes high because processing an item is locking the queue,\n                // and new items can't be added until processing finish.\n                // https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/103789\n                if depth > 10 {\n                        trace := utiltrace.New(\"DeltaFIFO Pop Process\",\n                                utiltrace.Field{Key: \"ID\", Value: id},\n                                utiltrace.Field{Key: \"Depth\", Value: depth},\n                                utiltrace.Field{Key: \"Reason\", Value: \"slow event handlers blocking the queue\"})\n                        defer trace.LogIfLong(100 * time.Millisecond)\n                }\n                err := process(item, isInInitialList)\n                if e, ok := err.(ErrRequeue); ok {\n                        f.addIfNotPresent(id, item)\n                        err = e.Err\n                }\n                // Don't need to copyDeltas here, because we're transferring\n                // ownership to the caller.\n                return item, err\n        }\n}\n\n// Replace atomically does two things: (1) it adds the given objects\n// using the Sync or Replace DeltaType and then (2) it does some deletions.\n// In particular: for every pre-existing key K that is not the key of\n// an object in `list` there is the effect of\n// `Delete(DeletedFinalStateUnknown{K, O})` where O is the latest known\n// object of K. The pre-existing keys are those in the union set of the keys in\n// `f.items` and `f.knownObjects` (if not nil). The last known object for key K is\n// the one present in the last delta in `f.items`. "func processDeltas(\n        // Object which receives event notifications from the given deltas\n        handler ResourceEventHandler,\n        clientState Store,\n        deltas Deltas,\n        isInInitialList bool,\n) error {\n        // from oldest to newest\n        for _, d := range deltas {\n                obj := d.Object\n\n                switch d.Type {\n                case Sync, Replaced, Added, Updated:\n                        if old, exists, err := clientState.Get(obj); err == nil && exists {\n                                if err := clientState.Update(obj); err != nil {\n                                        return err\n                                }\n                                handler.OnUpdate(old, obj)\n                        } else {\n                                if err := clientState.Add(obj); err != nil {\n                                        return err\n                                }\n                                handler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList)\n                        }\n                case Deleted:\n                        if err := clientState.Delete(obj); err != nil {\n                                return err\n                        }\n                        handler.OnDelete(obj)\n                }\n        }\n        return nil\n}\n\n// newInformer returns a controller for populating the store while also\n// providing event notifications.\n//\n// Parameters\n//   - clientState is the store you want to populate\n//   - options contain the options to configure the controller\nfunc newInformer(clientState Store, options InformerOptions) Controller {\n        // This will hold incoming changes. Note, however, that there is no promise about\n// ordering between states seen for different objects.\n//\n// The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\n// during `Run()`.\n//\n// As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\n// unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\n// collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\n// SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\n// collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\n// service ends, or communication problems between the two\n// persistently thwart achievement).\n//\n// As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\n// non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\n// removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\n// removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\n// too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\n// problems persistently thwart the desired result).\n//\n// The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\n// objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\n// Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\n// a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\n// into its constituent parts.\n//\n// Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\n// snapshot of the cache's state. "func (f *DeltaFIFO) queueActionLocked(actionType DeltaType, obj interface{}) error {\n        return f.queueActionInternalLocked(actionType, actionType, obj)\n}\n\n// queueActionInternalLocked appends to the delta list for the object.\n// The actionType is emitted and must honor emitDeltaTypeReplaced.\n// The internalActionType is only used within this function and must\n// ignore emitDeltaTypeReplaced.\n// Caller must lock first.\nfunc (f *DeltaFIFO) queueActionInternalLocked(actionType, internalActionType DeltaType, obj interface{}) error {\n        id, err := f.KeyOf(obj)\n        if err != nil {\n                return KeyError{obj, err}\n        }\n\n        // Every object comes through this code path once, so this is a good\n        // place to call the transform func.\n        //\n        // If obj is a DeletedFinalStateUnknown tombstone or the action is a Sync,\n        // then the object have already gone through the transformer.\n        //\n        // If the objects already present in the cache are passed to Replace(),\n        // the transformer must be idempotent to avoid re-mutating them,\n        // or coordinate with all readers from the cache to avoid data races.\n        // Default informers do not pass existing objects to Replace.\n        if f.transformer != nil {\n                _, isTombstone := obj.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown)\n                if !isTombstone && internalActionType != Sync {\n                        var err error\n                        obj, err = f.transformer(obj)\n                        if err != nil {\n                                return err\n                        }\n                }\n        }\n\n        oldDeltas := f.items[id]\n        newDeltas := append(oldDeltas, Delta{actionType, obj})\n        newDeltas = dedupDeltas(newDeltas)\n\n        if len(newDeltas) > 0 {\n                if _, exists := f.items[id]; !exists {\n                        f.queue = append(f.queue, id)\n                }\n                f.items[id] = newDeltas\n                f.cond.Broadcast()\n        } else {\n                // This never happens, because dedupDeltas never returns an empty list\n                // when given a non-empty list (as it is here).\n                // If somehow it happens anyway, deal with it but complain.\n                if oldDeltas == nil {\n                        klog.Errorf(\"Impossible dedupDeltas for id=%q: oldDeltas=%#+v, obj=%#+v; broke DeltaFIFO invariant by storing empty Deltas\", id, oldDeltas, obj)\n        }\n        return nil\n}\n\n// List returns a list of all the items; it returns the object\n// from the most recent Delta.\n// You should treat the items returned inside the deltas as immutable.\nfunc (f *DeltaFIFO) List() []interface{} {\n        f.lock.RLock()\n        defer f.lock.RUnlock()"

"func (f *DeltaFIFO) Add(obj interface{}) error {\n        f.lock.Lock()\n        defer f.lock.Unlock()\n        f.populated = true\n        return f.queueActionLocked(Added, obj)\n}\n\n// Update is just like Add, but makes an Updated Delta.\nfunc (f *DeltaFIFO) Update(obj interface{}) error {\n        f.lock.Lock()\n        defer f.lock.Unlock()\n        f.populated = true\n        return f.queueActionLocked(Updated, obj)\n}\n\n// Delete is just like Add, but makes a Deleted Delta. If the given\n// object does not already exist, it will be ignored. (It may have\n// already been deleted by a Replace (re-list), for example.)  In this\n// method `f.knownObjects`, if not nil, provides (via GetByKey)\n// _additional_ objects that are considered to already exist.\nfunc (f *DeltaFIFO) Delete(obj interface{}) error {\n        id, err := f.KeyOf(obj)\n        if err != nil {\n                return KeyError{obj, err}\n        }\n        f.lock.Lock()\n        defer f.lock.Unlock()\n        f.populated = true\n        if f.knownObjects == nil {\n                if _, exists := f.items[id]; !exists {\n                        // Presumably, this was deleted when a relist happened.\n                        // Don't provide a second report of the same deletion.\n                        return nil\n                }\n        } else {\n                // We only want to skip the \"deletion\" action if the object doesn't\n                // exist in knownObjects and it doesn't have corresponding item in items.\n                // Note that even if there is a \"deletion\" action in items, we can ignore it,\n                // because it will be deduped automatically in \"queueActionLocked\"\n                _, exists, err := f.knownObjects.GetByKey(id)\n                _, itemsExist := f.items[id]\n                if err == nil && !exists && !itemsExist {\n                        // Presumably, this was deleted when a relist happened.\n                        // Don't provide a second report of the same deletion.\n                        return nil\n                }\n        }\n\n        // exist in items and/or KnownObjects\n        return f.queueActionLocked(Deleted, obj)\n}\n\n// AddIfNotPresent inserts an item, and puts it in the queue. If the item is already\n// present in the set, it is neither enqueued nor added to the set.\n//\n// This is useful in a single producer/consumer scenario so that the consumer can\n// safely retry items without contending with the producer and potentially enqueueing\n// stale items.\n//\n// Important: obj must be a Deltas (the output of the Pop() function). Yes, this is\n// different from the Add/Update/Delete functions.\nfunc (f *DeltaFIFO) AddIfNotPresent(obj interface{}) error {\n        deltas, ok := obj.(Deltas)\n        if !ok {\n                return fmt.Errorf(\"object must be of type deltas, but got: %#v\", obj)\n        }\n        id, err := f.KeyOf(deltas)\n        if err != nil {\n                return KeyError{obj, err}\n        }\n        f.lock.Lock()\n        defer f.lock.Unlock()\n        f.addIfNotPresent(id, deltas)\n        return nil\n}\n\n// addIfNotPresent inserts deltas under id if it does not exist, and assumes the caller\n// already holds the fifo lock.\nfunc (f *DeltaFIFO) addIfNotPresent(id string, deltas Deltas) {\n        f.populated = true\n        if _, exists := f.items[id]; exists {\n                return\n        }\n\n        f.queue = append(f.queue, id)\n        f.items[id] = deltas\n        f.cond.Broadcast()\n}\n\n// re-listing and watching can deliver the same update multiple times in any\n// order. This will combine the most recent two deltas if they are the same.\nfunc dedupDeltas(deltas Deltas) Deltas {"

"func (r *Request) Watch(ctx context.Context) (watch.Interface, error) {\n        w, _, e := r.watchInternal(ctx)\n        return w, e\n}\n\nfunc (r *Request) watchInternal(ctx context.Context) (watch.Interface, runtime.Decoder, error) {\n        if r.body == nil {\n                logBody(ctx, 2, \"Request Body\", r.bodyBytes)\n        }\n\n        // We specifically don't want to rate limit watches, so we\n        // don't use r.rateLimiter here.\n        if r.err != nil {\n                return nil, nil, r.err\n        }\n\n        client := r.c.Client\n        if client == nil {\n                client = http.DefaultClient\n        }\n\n        isErrRetryableFunc := func(request *http.Request, err error) bool {\n                // The watch stream mechanism handles many common partial data errors, so closed\n                // connections can be retried in many cases.\n                if net.IsProbableEOF(err) || net.IsTimeout(err) {\n                        return true\n                }\n                return false\n        }\n        retry := r.retryFn(r.maxRetries)\n        url := r.URL().String()\n        for {\n                if err := retry.Before(ctx, r); "func (c *Cacher) processEvent(event *watchCacheEvent) {\n        if curLen := int64(len(c.incoming)); c.incomingHWM.Update(curLen) {\n                // Monitor if this gets backed up, and how "func (c *cacheWatcher) process(ctx context.Context, resourceVersion uint64) {\n        // At this point we already start processing incoming watch events.\n        // However, the init event can still be processed because their serialization\n        // and sending to the client happens asynchrnously.\n        // TODO: As describe in the KEP, we would like to estimate that by delaying\n        //   the initialization signal proportionally to the number of events to\n        //   process, but we're leaving this to the tuning phase.\n        utilflowcontrol.WatchInitialized(ctx)\n\n        for {\n                select {\n                case event, ok := <-c.input:\n                        if !ok {\n                                return\n                        }\n                        // only send events newer than resourceVersion\n                        // or a bookmark event with an RV equal to resourceVersion\n                        // if we haven't sent one to the client\n                        if event.ResourceVersion > resourceVersion || (event.Type == watch.Bookmark && event.ResourceVersion == resourceVersion && !c.wasBookmarkAfterRvSent()) {\n                                c.sendWatchCacheEvent(event)\n                        }\n                case <-ctx.Done():\n                        return\n                }\n        }\n}"

"func (c *Cacher) startCaching(stopChannel <-chan struct{}) {\n        // The 'usable' lock is always 'RLock'able when it is safe to use the cache.\n        // It is safe to use the cache after a successful list until a disconnection.\n        // We start with usable (write) locked. The below OnReplace function will\n        // unlock it after a successful list. The below defer will then re-lock\n        // it when this function exits (always due to disconnection), only if\n        // we actually got a successful list. This cycle will repeat as needed.\n        successfulList := false\n        c.watchCache.SetOnReplace(func() {\n                successfulList = true\n                c.ready.set(true)\n                klog.V(1).Infof(\"cacher (%v): initialized\", c.groupResource.String())\n                metrics.WatchCacheInitializations.WithLabelValues(c.groupResource.String()).Inc()\n        })\n        defer func() {\n                if successfulList {\n                        c.ready.set(false)\n                }\n        }()\n\n        c.terminateAllWatchers()\n        // Note that since onReplace may be not called due to errors, we explicitly\n        // need to retry it on errors under lock.\n        // Also note that startCaching is called in a loop, so there's no need\n        // to have another loop here.\n        if err := c.reflector.ListAndWatch(stopChannel); err != nil {\n                klog.Errorf(\"cacher (%v): unexpected ListAndWatch error: %v; reinitializing...\", c.groupResource.String(), err)\n        }\n}\n\n// Versioner implements storage.Interface.\nfunc (c *Cacher) Versioner() storage.Versioner {\n        return c.storage.Versioner()\n}\n\n// Create implements storage.Interface.\nfunc (c *Cacher) Create(ctx context.Context, key string, obj, out runtime.Object, ttl uint64) error {\n        return c.storage.Create(ctx, key, obj, out, ttl)\n}"

Whenever it receives any complete (Store.Replace) or incremental change\n    22  // (Store.Add, Store.Update, Store.Delete), it sends the complete state by calling PushFunc.\n    23  // It is thread-safe.  It guarantees that every change (Add, Update, Replace, Delete) results\n    24  // in one call to PushFunc, but sometimes PushFunc may be called twice with the same values.\n    25  // PushFunc should be thread safe.\n    26  type UndeltaStore struct {\n    27          Store\n    28          PushFunc func([]interface{})\n    29  }\n    30\n    31  // Assert that it implements the Store interface.\n    32  var _ Store = &UndeltaStore{}\n    33\n    34  // Add inserts an object into the store and sends complete state by calling PushFunc.\n    35  // Note about thread safety.  The Store implementation (cache.cache) uses a lock for all methods.\n    36  // In the functions below, the lock gets released and reacquired betweend the {Add,Delete,etc}\n    37  // and the List.  So, the following can happen, resulting in two identical calls to PushFunc.\n    38  // time            thread 1                  thread 2\n    39  // 0               UndeltaStore.Add(a)\n    40  // 1                                         UndeltaStore.Add(b)\n    41  // 2               Store.Add(a)\n    42  // 3                                         Store.Add(b)\n    43  // 4               Store.List() -> [a,b]\n    44  // 5                                         Store.List() -> [a,b]\n    45  func (u *UndeltaStore) Add(obj interface{}) error {\n    46          if err := u.Store.Add(obj); \"kubernetes/client-go\", \"path\": \"tools/cache/store.go\", \"symbol\": \"cache.Delete\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The Kubernetes informer cache event handler chain spans multiple repositories and layers. Here is the complete trace:\\n\\n## 1. API Server Storage Layer (kubernetes/kubernetes - staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver)\\n\\n### etcd3 Watch (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/watcher.go)\\nThe chain begins at `store.Watch()` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go`, which delegates to `watcher.Watch()`. This creates a `watchChan` struct and starts it via `watchChan.run()`. Inside `run()`, two goroutines are launched: `startWatching()` (which calls the etcd client's `Watch()` to receive raw etcd events, parses them via `parseEvent()`/`parseKV()`, and sends them to `incomingEventChan`) and `processEvents()` (which reads from `incomingEventChan`, calls `transform()` to decode objects, and sends `watch.Event` values to `resultChan`). The `watchChan` implements `watch.Interface` via `ResultChan()` and `Stop()`.\\n\\n### Cacher Layer (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/)\\nThe `Cacher` (`cacher.go`) wraps the etcd3 store with an in-memory watch cache. `NewCacherFromConfig()` creates:\\n- A `watchCache` (`watch_cache.go`) as the reflector's Store, with `cacher.processEvent` as its `eventHandler`\\n- A `listerWatcher` (`lister_watcher.go`) that implements `cache.ListerWatcher` backed by the etcd3 storage\\n- A `cache.Reflector` (from client-go) pointed at the `listerWatcher` and `watchCache`\\n\\n`startCaching()` calls `reflector.ListAndWatch()` to populate the watch cache. When the reflector calls `watchCache.Add/Update/Delete()`, `watchCache.processEvent()` updates the internal store and calls `eventHandler(wcEvent)` which is `cacher.processEvent()`. This sends the event to the `incoming` channel. The `dispatchEvents()` goroutine reads from `incoming` and calls `dispatchEvent()`, which fans out to all registered `cacheWatcher` instances via `nonblockingAdd()` and `add()`.\\n\\n`Cacher.Watch()` creates a `cacheWatcher` (`cache_watcher.go`), registers it, and starts `cacheWatcher.processInterval()` in a goroutine. This goroutine first drains historical events from a `watchCacheInterval`, then calls `cacheWatcher.process()` which reads from the `input` channel (fed by `dispatchEvent`). Both paths call `sendWatchCacheEvent()` \u2192 `convertToWatchEvent()` \u2192 sends `watch.Event` to `result` channel. The `cacheWatcher` implements `watch.Interface`.\\n\\n### HTTP Watch Handler (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/)\\n`ListResource()` in `get.go` handles incoming watch HTTP requests. When `opts.Watch` is true, it calls `rw.Watch()` (which reaches `Cacher.Watch()`) and then `serveWatchHandler()` in `watch.go`. This creates a `WatchServer` whose `HandleHTTP()` method reads events from `watch.Interface.ResultChan()` and writes them as chunked HTTP responses to the client.\\n\\n## 2. Watch Event Transport (kubernetes/kubernetes - staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/watch/)\\n\\n`watch.go` defines the `Interface` (with `ResultChan()` and `Stop()`) and `Event` struct. `streamwatcher.go` provides `StreamWatcher` which reads from an HTTP response body via a `Decoder`, decodes events in `receive()`, and sends them to its `result` channel. `mux.go` provides `Broadcaster` for server-side fan-out of watch events.\\n\\n## 3. Client-Side REST Watch (kubernetes/client-go - rest/)\\n\\n`Request.Watch()` in `rest/request.go` makes an HTTP GET request with `?watch=true`. On a 200 OK response, `newStreamWatcher()` creates a `watch.StreamWatcher` wrapping a `restclientwatch.Decoder` (`rest/watch/decoder.go`). The `Decoder.Decode()` method reads framed watch events from the HTTP stream and decodes them into `watch.Event` values.\\n\\n## 4. ListWatch (kubernetes/client-go - tools/cache/listwatch.go)\\n\\n`ListWatch` implements `ListerWatcher`. `NewListWatchFromClient()` / `NewFilteredListWatchFromClient()` create a `ListWatch` whose `Watch()` method calls `WatchFunc` which calls `Request.Watch()` on the REST client, returning a `StreamWatcher`. `List()` calls `ListFunc` which calls `Request.Do().Get()` for paginated listing.\\n\\n## 5. Reflector (kubernetes/client-go - tools/cache/reflector.go)\\n\\n`Reflector` is the core component that bridges the API server watch stream to the local Store. `Reflector.Run()` calls `ListAndWatch()` in a backoff loop. `ListAndWatch()` first calls `list()` (which uses `pager.ListPager` to paginate list calls, then calls `syncWith()` \u2192 `store.Replace()`) and then `watchWithResync()` \u2192 `watch()`. `watch()` calls `listerWatcher.Watch()` to get a `watch.Interface`, then calls `handleWatch()` \u2192 `handleAnyWatch()`. Inside `handleAnyWatch()`, a `for` loop reads from `w.ResultChan()` and dispatches:\\n- `watch.Added` \u2192 `store.Add(event.Object)`\\n- `watch.Modified` \u2192 `store.Update(event.Object)`\\n- `watch.Deleted` \u2192 `store.Delete(event.Object)`\\n\\nThe `store` here is a `DeltaFIFO`.\\n\\n## 6. DeltaFIFO Queue (kubernetes/client-go - tools/cache/delta_fifo.go)\\n\\n`DeltaFIFO` is a producer-consumer queue. `Add()`, `Update()`, `Delete()`, and `Replace()` (called by the Reflector) call `queueActionLocked()` \u2192 `queueActionInternalLocked()` which appends a `Delta` to the item's delta list and broadcasts to waiting consumers. `Pop(process)` blocks until an item is available, dequeues it, and calls the `process` function with the `Deltas`.\\n\\n## 7. Controller (kubernetes/client-go - tools/cache/controller.go)\\n\\n`controller.Run()` creates a `Reflector` with the `DeltaFIFO` as its store and starts `processLoop()`. `processLoop()` repeatedly calls `Queue.Pop(Process)` where `Process` is `HandleDeltas` (for SharedIndexInformer) or `processDeltas` (for basic informers). `processDeltas()` iterates over deltas and for each:\\n- `Sync/Replaced/Added/Updated`: calls `clientState.Update()` or `clientState.Add()` on the local cache, then `handler.OnUpdate()` or `handler.OnAdd()`\\n- `Deleted`: calls `clientState.Delete()`, then `handler.OnDelete()`\\n\\n## 8. SharedIndexInformer (kubernetes/client-go - tools/cache/shared_informer.go)\\n\\n`sharedIndexInformer.Run()` creates a `DeltaFIFO`, a `controller` (with `HandleDeltas` as the Process function), and starts the `sharedProcessor`. `HandleDeltas()` calls `processDeltas(s, s.indexer, deltas, isInInitialList)` where `s` (the `sharedIndexInformer`) acts as the `ResourceEventHandler`.\\n\\nWhen `processDeltas` calls `handler.OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete` on the `sharedIndexInformer`, these methods call `s.processor.distribute(notification, isSync)`. `sharedProcessor.distribute()` iterates over all registered `processorListener`s and calls `listener.add(notification)`, which sends to `addCh`.\\n\\nEach `processorListener` runs two goroutines:\\n- `pop()`: pumps notifications from `addCh` through a ring buffer to `nextCh`\\n- `run()`: reads from `nextCh` and calls the registered `ResourceEventHandler`'s `OnAdd()`, `OnUpdate()`, or `OnDelete()` methods\\n\\nUsers register handlers via `AddEventHandler()` / `AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod()`, which create `processorListener` instances wrapping the user's `ResourceEventHandler`.\\n\\n## 9. Local Cache Store (kubernetes/client-go - tools/cache/store.go, thread_safe_store.go)\\n\\nThe `cache` struct (implementing `Store`/`Indexer`) is backed by a `threadSafeMap` (`thread_safe_store.go`). `cache.Add/Update/Delete()` delegate to `threadSafeMap.Add/Update/Delete()` which update the in-memory map and maintain indices. This is the `clientState` / `s.indexer` used in `processDeltas`.\\n\\n## Summary of the Chain\\n\\netcd change \u2192 `watchChan.startWatching` (etcd3/watcher.go) \u2192 `watchChan.processEvents` \u2192 `watchChan.ResultChan()` \u2192 `WatchServer.HandleHTTP` (apiserver handlers/watch.go) \u2192 HTTP chunked response \u2192 `StreamWatcher.receive` (apimachinery/watch/streamwatcher.go) \u2192 `Decoder.Decode` (client-go/rest/watch/decoder.go) \u2192 `ListWatch.Watch` (client-go/tools/cache/listwatch.go) \u2192 `Reflector.watch` \u2192 `handleAnyWatch` (client-go/tools/cache/reflector.go) \u2192 `DeltaFIFO.Add/Update/Delete` (client-go/tools/cache/delta_fifo.go) \u2192 `DeltaFIFO.Pop` \u2192 `controller.processLoop` (client-go/tools/cache/controller.go) \u2192 `sharedIndexInformer.HandleDeltas` \u2192 `processDeltas` \u2192 `cache.Add/Update/Delete` (local store update) + `sharedIndexInformer.OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete` \u2192 `sharedProcessor.distribute` \u2192 `processorListener.add` \u2192 `processorListener.pop` \u2192 `processorListener.run` \u2192 `ResourceEventHandler.OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete` (user handler)\"\n}\n",
